Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	 We, and those of our time, place a compress plentifully soaked with oil.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if an instrument cannot enter the oil due to its hardness, for there are men who have very hard eyes, it is necessary that you use the tool called "alberit," of which here is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	 And thus pierce the conjunctiva only slightly, not too deeply but gently; then pour oil as we have said; and at the completion of the work prepare for the patient to rest with an agreeable bedding on his back in a dark place; he should avoid all movements, eat light meals, and do not move his head or limbs, keeping him secured according to his position until three days; then release him into a similar dark room, check his vision, show him various things, and put the bandage back for another seven days; it must be done at this time of treatment but not immediately after incision, as the blood rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	 If an abscess is present, you should drain it before the seventh day, and apply the remedy that soothes the abscess; and once it is calmed, close up the wound and cover with a cloth for several days, allowing it to remain in the dark room of that house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	 And then remove from the light and more light, and let it transform into its own thing; and be aware that no pupils should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	A man came to us from the Yrach who told us that in our land a strange occurrence took place where water would flow, but I have never seen it in our territory nor read of it in ancient books; and perhaps this is a new discovery.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	These are the forms that resemble Almagda, because those who do not know them see them thus; and they are indeed akin to rain.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And let the head of these beings have a similar subtlety, and their bodies in three corners with water.
de la char sor le neis	I; And it'fat;
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	 Never are births or various abscesses formed from it, some of which appear like scorpions with many legs; and if there are such or they have flesh of intense color, and it is soft in bone color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	 In that case for those chests which are hollow and not inflated, you must make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; work on their nostrils, pour the spittle into them, and cleanse with a fork; so tie what you support at the subtle narrow part of a feather, as long as you know that chest is entirely ossified.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any part that cannot be covered, work all the subtle points lightly, such that nothing is left; and if it forms a bump or abscess as it should, then treat it accordingly; and if they are malignant abscesscups, haste to cauterize until it is fully healed and all cartilage parts are turned to bone, then pour oil or vinegar or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	 If the remedy does not work and moisture reaches the palate, know that it is safe; if the moisture does not break as it should, know that there is hollow bone above, where inflammation cannot come to cut: then you must tie a linen thread of moderate thickness between your hands, leaving some space between each finger; and place the patient's head with the thread in their nostril at most strength, pulling gently until it comes out through the nose into the mouth; this is often done for children in schools, and it is an easy thing for those who know how to do it; then hold the head that emerges from one nostril with one hand, and the other head that emerges from the mouth with the other hand, alternating as the thread passes through our fingers.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	 Do what you know will help the children whose veins have been corrupted, then pierce the child's flesh, draw out blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian unguent. Place it back in its rightful place as before; do this for three days or more until the ointment has dissolved all that is attached to the vein; afterwards, put a bandage of linen on without any delay until they are healthy again, and if there's need for dry medicines, use them; this is the method used with an instrument designed to purge the head through which oils and medicines are distilled.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And make it of silver or brass, like an open lantern, as with a panhandle, and guide in the same manner; and if you see, then create a closed handle for the purpose of expelling from the head; and have one handle on the head to hold when heating oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	I; And it'fat;
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times arises in the head of the neck a disease called "telul", which grows and becomes large until it is visible to the eye; therefore, one must begin by cutting out entirely, then apply hot caustic or burning medicine; if not treated promptly as it grows, be aware if it's hard, discolored, with poor sensation: do not treat with iron as it is an incurable boil, for when cut once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the boil is from a sensitive touch, without discoloration, and you see that one can cover it entirely, then relieve the patient of fear and anxiety while treating drying and tightening matters.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the neck is cut and caused by this,
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	 Believes that when continuous treatments occur in one of these delicate cartilages, it benefits little and even harms some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then you must indeed when this occurs in any case, look to see if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then approach it for stitching as soon as possible; and if the edges are already torn apart on both sides, it is necessary that you scrape off all parts of their core until they heal, then join the edges by sewing them together, apply a bandage, and powder with blood powder from a dragon's blood, and burned incense; and place over the powders a piece of lead oxide or another similar substance so that it melts through, then treat with ointment until healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of suturing is such that you assemble the stitches: either with needles, as we have said in the abdominal wound treatment; or with thread, as I have instructed you before.
des apostemes des levres	For abscesses on the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	For abscesses on the lips that occur hard like grains of barley, small and larger; then it is necessary to turn the lips over, make incisions above each one, take with forceps and tie into sections; afterwards apply vinegar after lithontriptor incision until bleeding stops; then soothe with a salve, and treat the wound area until healed.
de la char des gencives	From the gum of teeth
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often there is swelling above the gums, which the ancients called 'albulus'; it must be held with forceps, cut to its root and allow blood or pus to flow out; then apply vitriol paste or other powders that are restraining and drying. If the abscess returns after incision, sometimes requiring a second enucleation and cauterization; if it does not return after cautionery, these are methods for treating ulcers.
des sordens	From scurves
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	At times they are assembled in the head of the gums, within the mouth between the gums, unsightly and sharp scales; at no time are teeth black and yellowish-green and pungent until corruption comes to the gum, and teeth become foul-smelling. It is necessary that you make the patient sit with their head in your hand, and his eyes in your holy place, and remove any teeth or scales found, as long as nothing remains; thus treat discoloration and greening, yellowing, and other afflictangs until they are healed; if what was removed at first treatment is still present, it's good; otherwise, begin anew on the second day and then every third day until everything is gone; know that teeth require various forms of dressings to heal, according to how the work shows, because those who fail to extract gums have different shapes than those extracted between them; these shapes and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when treating the tooth's pain that you delay with the drilling as long as possible, because it should not be done at all; for it's a substance very deep until there is no excuse for extraction.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	 Then when the patient is strained from milking, you must be certain of the pain in their teeth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	 Many times the pain troubles the patient, and they believe it is a toothache and extract the bad tooth; yet never does the pain depart for this reason, as long as the evil winds are present, because we have already made them do so with these saints (herbs); and when you are well certain of the aching tooth, it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth thoroughly to protect the gum on all sides; then move it back with your fingers or pliers delicately at first touch by touch until it is properly aligned, then firmly secure the pliers; and let the head of the shoulder be in its proper place between your knees, and hold it tight so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	 After extracting the tooth straight and breaking it, if it does not immediately fall out, take one of these antidotes and pour into each part gently, and move it just as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	 And if the tooth is pierced and infected, you must fill it with rags where the roots are; and gently extract it with pliers so that it does not break while being extracted; and work skillfully around the gum to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	 And be careful not to break it and leave a part behind, as this may cause the patient greater pain from the root's evil nature.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	 And be wary not to do as ignorant barbers do, who hastily and recklessly break the root every time without heed, nor apply what we have mentioned; rather they often bring about great disease from the roots that remain or from breaking the root itself, as we have seen frequently happen. When extracting a tooth, wash its socket with wine or herbs and salt; if bleeding occurs, which is common, fill it with broth of alum powder; if this does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the substances that numb the nerves first are those with sharp points and large knobs, which do not double when you extract the tooth; these are the ingredients:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them have large limbs that do not bend at the joints, and be made of well-forged iron, and equipped with teeth to hold together.
de la racine des dens	From the root of the teeth

et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is like the grinding of needles; and gently grind the tooth little by little, so that it does not move until it becomes sharp; then in the end smooth out any roughness completely, and if it is too sharp and cuts the tongue, then grind the sharp edge until it is even, so that it neither cuts the tongue nor corrupts speech.
quant li dent lochent	When a tooth chips or breaks: take some wax of aloes, and melt it well in boiling water; when it is liquid, pour it into the hole and press the broken part against it until it sets, so that no food will enter. Then you can grind down the protruding edge as mentioned above.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	 When the tooth is loose or cracked by hitting or falling out, and the patient cannot press down on what they chew without salivation, cured with medicines that restrict but do not work; if needed, restrain it with a gold wire because silver wire becomes green and rusts, but gold never changes. Make sure the wire is of medium thickness according to the space between the teeth; and if you see them aligning properly, take the wire and tie it double around two healthy teeth, then place the loose tooth between the aligned ones, with additional wires if necessary, until securely in position on the other side. Repeat the process of covering up to where you started, gently and skillfully pulling outward without moving; ensure your grip is firm at the root so it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	 Then close the head with a wire using pliers, joining them together and placing between healthy teeth so it does not touch the tongue; then leave it as tightly closed as possible, if it dislocates or wires break, strain an additional filament; if kept intact, it will serve for its intended duration, forming the shape of two healthy teeth and mimicking their structure:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens. li chapistres des apostemes	The form of this instrument used to treat sinuses; it is similar to the throat resembles an apothecary's spoon and has a rough surface for enters like limestone, so whatever that takes in cannot satiated. Its design:
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	 There are many kinds of abscesses, as shown in this book with examples from one and another, and they differ in perforation and cutting; there are two ways to treat them, one is the same kind that takes moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	 And the second way is for wounds where they lie within the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	 For an abscess at the top is different from one at the base, and an abscess in fibrous tissue is different from those occurring in joints, each has its judgment in practice.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	 And if one encounters an abscess that should not be pierced until it is fully formed; and for those that need to be pierced when they are ripe, but do not mature as expected, like abscesses near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	 When abscesses arise near joints and are left to persist until they rot away, sometimes the ligaments and nerves of the joint may become corrupted, causing contractures in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	 If the abscess is near a major limb and you delay perforation until it dies, it will harm the main limb; if it is near the base, pierce as soon as possible before it dies. It should only be pierced when digestion of the abscess is complete, especially if near the base, preventing spread in all directions, and allowing drainage within, and a fistula forms; it cannot heal fully for a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	 When an abscess is formed in place, it must be left to bleed until the process of complete digestion has been achieved, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	 And if to any abscess that is pierced according to the width of his body, depending on what the limb requires.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	 And it is necessary to close small abscesses with small punctures; and for large abscessebs, larger punctures, along with multiple incisions according to the size of the abscess; and if such an abscess requires cutting off the top or covering it up when it has become as soft as cloth and fallen apart, then do so as one would with bottles: and for those that are split into three angles, or punctured like a marten's fur sack, similar to arm-pit abscesses; and for those where a circular incision is made, along with other types of incisions.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	 Those who have no head like a superficial abscess, it must be punctured easily; and when the abscess is large, and has great swelling, and you puncture it, do not milk out all the pus at once, but drain only part of it; then bandage the abscess until the next day, then leave nothing else to be drained; perform this repeatedly over time increasingly so that all the pus is released; especially if the patient is weak in strength, or women bearing children, or small children, or old decrepit men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	 For the abscess may sometimes burst with the release of pus, which could cause the patient's death, and do not be dismayed by this.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Therefore treat this chapter with great caution, and when you have located your abscess, open the wound and check if the abscess is small; and if it is a clean cut, dress it with linen or old cotton; and if it is large abscesses and there are many hairs, ensure that each tent touches another so they adhere to each other; and if you have sewn an area near the skin in the abscess, fill it with old cotton or linen thread without moisture, until three days pass; then visit a physician and treat with ointment until healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	 If blood flow arises from your wound, treat it with cold and soothing water, and apply wet bandages, and place them on the affected area repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the bleeding persists, treat it with proper care and remedies mentioned in this book, and if it's winter or the place of abscess is very sensitive, cover tents and moistened cloths soaked in wine and hot oil; and if it's summer, and the affected area is fleshy, use dampened cloths soaked in cold water and oil, or vinegar and cooling oil until after three days as we have said; then remove the abscess, express pus, and continue treatment until it becomes healthy.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know universally for the treatment of abscesses; now I have told you how one should proceed before treating abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	Of pus-filled sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	 When small abscesses appear on the head and have ways that resemble cords like those of a lamb's bladder, there are many similarities.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	 There are some that are fatty and mucous like hairs; and there are others that are hard and painful to touch when cut, and without doubt they do not react if the arrow strikes them.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	 And the treatments for hare lips are such that you must touch with every instrument called 'intermixed', from which its shape comes afterward and what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	 For if they contain moisture, then the hairs fall down on top.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	 And when the moisture is emptied, they scrape it without leaving any hair that contains the moisture behind, because it returns as soon as nothing is left; then soak a cotton in Egyptian ointment if present; otherwise, use water and salt, and apply to the wound until tomorrow; this is how you treat those that have been overnight.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Begin the cotton again as before, on the second day and thereafter, until you are certain it does not remain out all night; then treat the wound with suitable ointment until healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	 If the abscess is very greasy, follow this procedure as long as needed: drain pus and apply bandages all around, treat any scrapes with care, and attend to the entire wound; if an arrow strikes you differently, do what I have previously instructed.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	 Do the same for a pus-filled abscess and perform cleaning as mentioned before.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	 For an arid and wet abscess, proceed more gently, as there is little blood involved.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	 In cases of these abscesses or heads where there is no moisture, and among those that I have opened in the head of an old woman; and found the abscess as hard as a stone, sharp and bruised, unable to be broken; if one had struck it, they would have made a wound like from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	 In other abscesses or heads that come from the head of children and roots of ears, ensure the opening is kept as low as possible for long periods so they can heal properly, and treat them accordingly.
des scrophules	Of scrofulas (tuberculous swellings of lymeboards)
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	 Many times abscesses occur in the neck, and from joints, and elbows, and never come elsewhere or body parts, and are very large, and intertwined with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	 There are some that contain moisture, and others that are malignant and do not wish to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	 In the case where you see good disposition upon touching, and it appears like the color of the body, is soft from all sides and not spongy to the nerves or arteries nor veins, and shallow; then it must be incised above, and skinned on each side, and extended skin around the edges as needed for abscesses on the head as we have said before; and pull gently little by little, being careful not to cut the nerve or vessel, and that there is no spatulaceous or penetrating tissue which might escape the hands, nor pulling too far forward so you do not incise what must be incised.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	 If you puncture the vein or artery and it does not allow you to work, then place vitriol paste into the wound, or any powders that remain blood inside, tighten the wound; let it be until the abscess is calmed, softened, the wound begins to decay.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	 And when blood is retained, return to your task until completed; then examine with your finger if there are no small scrofulous sores, cut and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	 If there is a large vein at the root of the scrofulous sore, do not cut that sore at its root, but bind it with a strong double thread and let it hang freely without harm; then treat the wound with gauze soaked in Egyptian ointment, then heal.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	 And if you cut the scrofula entirely, it is necessary to join the two edges of the wound and sew them up without leaving excess for the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	 And if it is necessary to cut near the root and draw out the pus, then sew as we have mentioned.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For scrofulas with excess buildup, pierce where it begins to fester; and pierce in the same way as previously mentioned, depending on this, then dress wounds with ointment and similar substances, so that what remains infected is preserved from corruption; and when the wound is thoroughly cleaned, apply an antiseptic balm until healed.
de squinance	And if you need to apply as needed for heals, but pus infection or inflammation, then wash oil again. Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and wrote of throat surgery; but I have never seen such a thing in our land, and this is the record of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those with epiglottitis, it is necessary to make an incision in the throat called "epiglotte"; and one does not help by doing so because all blood vessels and the main vein of the ailing are affected where abscesses heat up in the mouth or in the throat or in two fists.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the main vein, it is necessary to cope with the epiglottis to avoid the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	 When we wish to split the epiglottis, let us do so above three circles or between two by making a small slit across, between the two circles or through the quantity of the slit into the sacculus; and those eyes are suitable for sectioning the epiglottis with no spitting, and the vessels are long enough.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	 And if the master is fearful, it should be that he extends the skin of the throat to the entire oncine (probably a typo for 'oncet', meaning once or at once), then split the flesh as far as reaches the windpipe; and drain the vessels of blood, provided you see no other issues, and then close up the sacculus, as we have said; and it is shown by the fluid section of the windpipe which escapes through the opening that is broken, and due to the lack of voice; leave the open wound exposed.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour of doubt about strangulation has passed, bring together the two lips of the wound at its opening, and sew them with thread that adheres to tissue; then apply remedies which cause flesh to grow until it is sound again.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Until you completely clear out the throat, and the patient is judged close to death, and there's no remedy available.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	 Then you shall cover the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe through it, and he breathes through the wound, thus preventing death; and so they command to leave the open wound until the illness has passed, which takes 3 or 4 days, then they order to sew up the wound and cleanse it until cured; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	 I saw that a maiden was stabbed with a knife in her throat and pierced part of the windpipe; and I went to call for help to cure it, and found it as if she were dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found blood that had come from it, and clearly, it had not eaten vein or carried food other than throat fluid, and the wind came forth through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	 I hurried and sewed the ward, and cleansed it until it was healed; and nothing happened to the maiden but that she regained her voice, and returned afterward to normality; therefore I say there is no cause for fear in treating the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	Of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	 These abscesses are called "throat hernias," and they are large abscesses of the color of jet, and mostly occur in women; and there are two ways: natural and accidental; where nature has no remedy.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 And the accidental type is in two ways: one resembles fatty tissue and the other resembles an abscess that comes from artery; there is fear, and it does not matter to work on furrows unless they are small, and try them all thoroughly: if you find them as we did with fat, without attaching to any vein, then cover them like a nail, twisting them off entirely, and search well, and treat them as needed until they are perfectly healed.
des nous	And thus we.
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	 There are many ways to heal us, which I will describe all the resemblances; and it must now be told of all the differences that exist between our approach and their practice.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that it is fever and heat-stricken until the inflammation has passed, and the putrefaction is complete; then rests both fever and heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	 With our body having neither heat nor fever nor pain, and containing pus, which is its own sacules and follows the color of the body, beginning as hard as a bead, and becoming larger; and they have two resemblances, either grease or moisture, and the colors are such as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary when you come to the treatment of ours that you examine and inquire first about all the instruments called "intermixtures," according to what their form will be or procedure, which is afterward.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	 And the manner of probing an abscess in us is that you grasp or find more moisture there where you think it to be in the abscess, and turn its edges gently, until you know that the swelling has been felt by touch, then extract the intruder; but take care that nothing flies out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	 If moisture runs out from the ulcer, and it has a certain color as I have said about other abscesses; and if after inserting an object there is no moisture, know that it is fatty, so treat it as described for others with cross-shaped incision, taking hold of it at each end, and lightly scraping off from each side while keeping the covering where it lies clean using a piece of cloth; and if you cannot make it clean, then cut it into pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	 If nothing remains after it is cut out many times; and if a little is left, causing no great pain, then apply the wound with corrosive powders of alum water, press the wound, and apply soothing substances for other treatments until healed; and if it is large, sew up the edges of the wound, and cure using a remedy that cleanses deeply.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if it is contrary or something else, haste and apply the powder of vitriol to it, leave for two days or three until the wound heals, then let it rest from bleeding; afterwards return to what was delayed earlier.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	 See here the forms of intrusion wafers, and they are in three ways: large, medium, and small; and there are three parts called "albaret," and one called "breb," and there are three ways: large, medium, and small, to pursue abscesses from fistulas; and like the needles with which we sew spells, they come in citrine copper, iron, or silver, and those that move well are of yellow color, while for treating melancholic fistulas, more tested ones have a black hue; and there are three sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu. And the ancients said that it is made like a joint being assembled with screws, in such a way that you bind the threads after measuring slightly below the edge; then cut me here and treat the abscess of what works there until the threads fall off; and heal it as we have said, until it is perfectly healthy.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	 It never comes to rupturing the anuses as we have said, and opening them; nor do any of the intestines come out through the joints, and if they do, it is little, and they heal fully every hour; however, if it remains too long in this point, a fistula or abscess forms until the intestines protrude; and this happens by the extension of the abscess which is within the anuses as we have said, because they are stretched, then softened and swoln the holes and opened; and heal it so with cautery, as we have previously mentioned: and it is never sutured with iron in this manner: that the patient lies on his back between your hands, then cut the swollen skin of the wound according to the amount of three stitches; then extract the abscess which is below the skin layer, then take a thread and place it over the wound corresponding to the abscess on the head of the thready, and pull both ends; then extract the head of the thread, and do not close up the abscess or extend the opening nor any other thing as I have previously instructed you in the treatment of intestinal joints; then heal it with wound care.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And when you bind the wounds, clean them and treat the injury until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The sac is restricted, and has no appearance in the route, and the fire cautery becomes loose at this place, and closer to health.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	From the softening of the leather thongs
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the leather of the thongs is softened in certain people because the wheels that are within them become softened and sweat; and when one wishes to cleanse it, one makes the patient lie on their back with the coat beneath them, and cuts off the softened leather from the natural skin; then join the two edges into a seam, and as you see first remove the excess softened leather in three or four firm stitches; then clip between the stitches, and cure it as other wounds until it is healthy again, and let him sweat.
dou chastrement	From the breaking of
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	 I declare that stabling is abolished by our law, and for this reason, I do not wish to speak of it in this book; however, there are two reasons why it is necessary: the first being so that one can learn from a master's response when asked about care, and the second because we often need the taming of various beasts to assist us, such as goats, sheep, horses, and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	 I say then that taming is done in two ways: by attraction or by force.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus. Then treat the wound until it is healed.

de la tentigene	From strain or tension
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 If it is necessary to attempt, as we have said earlier, and treat until healed.
de erratique	Erratic stones are those that move or fall from their place without apparent cause; they can bring misfortune or illness according to the beliefs of some people at the time this text was written.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	 If the signs of ectopic pregnan([[*]]) are appearing, they can be on either thigh or groin. ([[*]]: Ectopic pregnancy is not known in medieval times but the location implies something

des emorroides	Here comes the translation of the text:
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	 I say that boils and ulcers, when they are fully formed in a knot, do not show to touch but can be treated with iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	 Those that are at the mouth of the knot, those one can feel and treat.

Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	 And if she becomes unwell, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu. de l’enfantement	Of childbirth

Then examine those flawed vessels that appear like an eagle's feather, leaving nothing behind.

Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	When restored, it is made whole and does not return.

Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	 A formication is a small false appearance across the body, and extends widely; and never feels cold, and it feels just like deathly tremors, spreading throughout the entire body, and more in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines. de la plaie dou col	If you have the body, then take the mots it is as it after the wounds the poisons and sins of be them all so that l'eux in the les bleeds now tear; and do not let me tains the hand.
