des voinnes dou cors communes	From the veins of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	 The veins which can be seen are XXXI in number, of which there are head XVI, that is: two hammers located behind the ears, called "herbech"; and the two arteries visible in both temples; and the two veins found within the eyelids, known as "aspires"; and the vein amidst the forehead; and the vein atop the nose bridge; and the two jugulars located on either side of the neck; and the two veins situated over the lips above the mouth, which are called "augeherich"; and the veins found below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	 In every arm there are commonly two veins: one is cephalic, and is on the left side of the neck; they call it by people "vein of the head"; and the other is called 'facile', composed of cephalic and basilica, and called by people "vein of the body"; the basilica lies on the right side of the neck, called by people "vein of the abdomen", and it is below the collarbone, and that vein one sees clearly upon palpation.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	 And the salvatic vein is the one between the little finger and the ring finger, with two branches; in the leg where the foot is, there are three veins: one is above the hollow of the calf on the left side of the neck, and the second saphenous which is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein called 'nesse', that is in the ankle of the other leg; and on the other leg are three veins as well.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	 The source of the veins that are behind the ears aids in ancient parchments and migraines; and its quality is as I have told you, and it involves raising the patient's head and rubbing their temples with rough cloth; then presses the neck with one finger until the two veins appear behind the ears, divided by two on each side of the head: therefore clasp them with your thumbs, and where you feel hair atop your thumbs, grip tightly; then take the lancet, and push it through to the bone below the vein, then place your hand over the entire vein area above, and scrape off the skin and vein well on both sides of its track, allowing blood flow until you see enough; then strain and bind, until it is healed; and I have already mentioned incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	 The vein of the two arteries that are in the temples, if old and swollen, thickened and accustomed to crying, with tears in their eyes; the qualities of this vein are as I describe: the patient is strangling his neck until the veins appear openly; he feels pain in his shoulders, then chokes on them; then lift your head towards your index finger above the vein, and place the lancet below it, extract the vein upwards, and follow with a bandage as you did with other veins, bleed according to your necessity; after that, lay the patient down, and put cotton on for an hour, then form it properly, leave it until healed; we have often spoken of their swelling and extraction, where this begins in the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	 The sinus of the vein on the forehead is as valuable for treating head diseases from ancient times, such as migraines and redness; its quality lies in that it allows patients to turn their neck by twisting until the veins appear. Then take the instrument called a "fosser," which has this form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	 And place the point over the vein, and sharpen it with your hand or another tool, allowing blood to flow out according to the amount you see; then release the patient's neck, and tie off the vein so that the wound heals cleanly without a wide scar being formed.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it must not be too tight with the bandage; and if the vein crosses, because the bone is close by, and at times the bandage breaks when it is too thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	 The sinus of the veins that are in the temples helps with eye-related issues, redness, and facial diseases; its quality lies in allowing patients to turn their neck by twisting without any ligaments being used, as before. Then sterilize it, and make the incision of the eyebrow a short distance long and slightly wide, for there is no pain involved.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the gaps are subtle and may be broken; then dose the blood, however much you need, and afterwards apply a poultice and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	 The condition of the vein in the neck is like a swelling, and itching and other facial illnesses such as migraines and rashes that come on the face, especially when they are longstanding; and the qualities of the affliction are such that the patient pulls his collar tight, then strains his neck to your left hand, and takes a fine, long breath, and inserts it into the space between the two nostrils because the vein does not open well on its own, and the blood begins to flow immediately; and do not make it too large, and cause the blood to flow according to your need, then bandage it for a night, as it is quickly restored; this is the form of the breath.
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	 The straining of the strings aids in stretching the joints, and at the beginning of melee practice, and for many diseases, and impetigo, and corrodents, and herpes, and itchiness; and the nature of the strain is such that the afflicted pull away his collar from both sides, as we have said; and let the master be standing over the sick person's head, and the patient squeeebox on a seat, then wipe the veins generously with a cloth, then quickly press out the blood as needed; then repeat in the other vein, then tie off the ligaments moderately, so that the afflicted cannot strangle themselves; and leave them until morning, when the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	 of the sinews of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	For the healing of sores in the mouth, and gum disease, and lip splits and ulcers and wounds, and burns within.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	 And the quality of these sinews is to have the patient sit before you, and strangle his neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, recognizing them by their blackness and the small dark vessels around them: so sever each of them. If you do not recognize them, or if you are in doubt, cut off the larger portion from each side, and similarly with all veins above and below, for they are made the same way.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	 of the sinews underneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	 The sinews under the veins of the tongue help after the cranial sinew, and they are at the extension of the throat, and with diseases of the eye, and mouth ailments; and its quality to sever is that the patient should hold between your hands facing the sunlight, lift the tongue, and look under each side for a black vein: so sever both, but not too deeply, as they are arteries from below.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	 The veins of the arm that are commonly bled follow two methods: either by puncturing at any wide spot, or with an olive-sized needle fine like sharp scissors, and they are called "anesil"; they are wide and fine according to the width and extension of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the worm-like swelling is very famous, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	 And it is necessary to open thick-skinned veins containing abundant and turbid blood, and this is the form of the olive-sized needle.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more subtle pointed, and is for collecting fine veins where there is subtle lemon-colored blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	 The bleeding of the basilic vein, which is one of these veins, assists with diseases that are below the throat, neck, groin, and abdomen; and it requires the leech to suck strongly, and cleanse itself of the artery below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	 If it cuts the artery and blood flow increases, if clotting is necessary, as I have said; but the flame must not be pinched, but trimmed as one sews.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	 And if the bandage does not open clearly, you must remove it and change to another; or you want no blood from it, or you sew into place within its vein in the arm: it opens clearly; and trim the flame as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	 And if you know the place of the injury, then stretch out the arm as much as necessary to see the hairs; then bandage the wound and then bind the arm, and trim the vein with flame as we have said; be careful not to hit the artery when you see it swelling because that is an artery: avoid this.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If you see it protrude upward like a child's urine, and the wound is red and fine, know that it is from an artery: hurry then, and extend your finger for a long time, after which remove your finger if it becomes untied; as often happens; do this to the arm, leave it thus, and don't move it until the patient feels at ease.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	If the wound is not stitched up, and it bleeds, and medicines are not prescribed, cut the artery if open, for the head of the wound contracts; thus, bind the wound.

Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	 Ventosation occurring in the neck is located between the esophagus and the basilic vein, and therefore it extends to the area of the throat, and splitting of the channel of the pharynx, and all around, and fullness; and one must not press too firmly, for if held too tightly, it may cause obstruction or stomach and body.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	 Ventosation in the ribs of the neck if it causes pain in the head, otalgia and migraine, and strangulation, and pain in the root of the teeth, and is located near the esophagus; and you must instruct the surgeon to express his hand while putting on a bandage so he does not cut an artery or cause bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	Ventilation near the chin causes diseases of the mouth, and decay of gums, and similar illnesses within the mouth; it is in the region of the sanctuaturi de l’orifice du ventre, et as dolors dou flanc qui est par le nerfs des costez.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The whitening of shoulders signifies an illness arising from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	 The inflammations of the elbows are as much as from III veins in the arm, because they draw blood from these large veins; and instruct the surgeon not to cut too deeply, for the flesh is close-grained, and knows nerves and arteries beneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The bladder that is above the rump is for hemorrhoids and diseases beneath it, and it must be large, made of wool, requiring thorough milking; and sometimes if it were too fine, it would break, causing great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The bladders for the legs cleanse openly because they draw blood from all over the body and are effective against ancient pains of the knees, hips, and bladder, and alleviate symptoms; they also weaken the body after prolonged use in certain positions, bringing about swelling in various conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying the cupping is that you first place it empty and do so promptly, apply quickly, move equally, and continue without stopping until you see the spot turn red and swell, with a reddish color from blood: then release, remove the cups, and be aware of the condition of the body, for there are those who have tender flesh and clear pores; thus it is necessary to strike once only, making wide and somewhat deep incisions, and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood vessel is large, it should be struck twice: the first time to thin out the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vessel is very dense, it should be struck a third time; and when we want to draw out blood little by little, we only strike once at most.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	 And if we want a lot of blood, let us reopen frequently; and if the wound is shallow, cut deeply, and make sure to pierce the center quickly, and it should be for those with thick skin and hard, who are easily pricked, apply ointments from oil that are aperitive and dissolving: if this is so, violet oil, or almond oil, or seed of cucurbite; and if green, watercress oil, or lily, or camomile, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	If there is excessive swelling that is large and cold, take oil of myrrh, or balmmyrtle oil, or aniseed oil, and similar substances.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	 And if for the one whom you treat with a tender and wide wound, there is no need to put oil on it; instead, after ventosating (washing) with rose water, cold water, or mallow water, cucurbite juice, porcelain pitcher water, or any similar substance.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	by *t and there; The same* archu (pris the telle;
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	 And those with large excesses rise from old wine, mallow water, or anise and chamomile decoction, or any similar substance; they should not apply a poultice before the bath nor after the bath but two hours after the bath; they must not sleep after ventosation (washing), and it is necessary that they sweat when to be ventosated and when ventosated.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	 And beware for those who have a cold illness and whose blood is too heated and inflamed; it is necessary that they ingest cool things, such as pomegranates, endives, lettuces easily prepared, similar items; mint sauce, chestnut charcuterie, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	 And those with a cold complexion should ingest honey syrup and fragrant wine that is neither old nor new, along with small porridges, mint sauce, small birds, pigeons; and for the days they will fast, they must drink more than eat; it is advisable to give certain individuals triaicle or muscat occasionally before ventosation or afterwards, to strengthen the main limbs; but dilution of the blood should only be done for those who are overheated.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	 The suction cups that are applied without causing harm are those placed on the liver, and kidneys, and gout, and stomach, and bowels, and legs and joints, for that limb cannot be harmed by any part being pierced; it is done solecuously to draw blood from one member to another as when we apply them to nipples when they are unwell; to remove the viscosity that is in the limb, as we apply suction cups on the stomach and bowels to reduce the size of the limb; and it relieves pain, when there is obstruction or stones, so by its attractive property it may possibly alleviate the obstruction, or remove the stone from its place; thus it acts when placed on the liver and kidneys when there is retained ventosity, and these suction cups are arranged empty to draw as much fluid; and at no time are they arranged together with fire, nor always filled with plain water, as in diseases of excessive sweating, and thus one fills the suction cup with hot water or water that has been boiled with suitable herbs for this purpose.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of administering fire to the blister is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	 And it should have two handles each half a palm thick at the base, and around the hollow of the mill a small hole, as for pushing in a needle, made of brass or iron, so that it does not slip on the patient's limb; and there should be in the middle a rod across of brass or iron to hold a lamp attached, and they come in large and small sizes according to the diseases and conditions of those who take them, for children's cupping sets are different from adults', and thinner than fattier.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	 And this is how you should place the cupping set on the limb: take a wax candle or lubricant and insert it through the rod which is across the ventose, ensuring that the flame does not burn the patient at the bottom of the ventose; then place it on the limb, with the handles as previously described so when you wish to, steam comes off, and remove the ventose. Take lubricant again as before, and start over frequently if needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	 In the suction cup method used for pleurisy treatment at once has no penis or scrotum and is only applied when full of water, placed on the limb thoroughly; this is its form.
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	 Without suction cups being applied except in limbs where you cannot place them due to their small size, such as lips and gums, or similar areas; also in open sores from chafing like cracks or nicks, and other similar issues. The quality of using them is that when you find suction cups filled with soft, clear waters without any foulness, take them; place them into a pool of soft water until they are swollen, having nothing in their bellies; then drain the vein and the cup, rub the limb until it becomes red, and apply the cups. When they become full and stick to the skin, if you can place a suction cup there, do so, as this method is most effective later on.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	 If not, raise the limb to aid its healing, then soak thoroughly in water, quite well, and then press; and if the veins swell too much after being used by the body without rest, moisten a linen cloth in cold water, and apply it until the swelling subsides; and if there are multiple swellings, use powdered stibnite or guaiacum, and similar substances, until they subside; or place half of a peeled onion over the joint, leave it until it dries to the skin, now it will be contained; and if you need more, take additional swellings.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	 If the swellings do not subside, rub the blood-soaked area with fresh blood or insert a needle until it draws out, and then place something over it; and when they feel heat from the blood, let them dry; and when you see that they are oozing, sprinkle some aloe vera and crushed seal oil, or ash, which will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	These chapters are often necessary in the art of medicine, and they involve the repair and replenishment of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	 Learn from this treatise, dear student, that the wise physician draws from its wisdom; they have never seen such teachings in any ancient books or letters read by them. And so the science is rare on our land, for I have found no good examples; I know nothing unless through the knowledge of ancient texts which I have studied extens groso and processed, as well as experimentation and the customs of my life; and herein I have described what this chapter contains, shortened it at the end, and clearly shown the methods for treating ailments as demonstrated in these two preceding chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, we must say that in this book are the summits of speech and chapters wherein the wise place their understanding, staying on truth so those experienced may know and learn this noble art and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	 I say that when fracture or dislocation or twisting or sprain occurs in any part of the body, it is necessary to support the patient on both sides if nothing completely holds them, as with weak limbs or infants or elderly; or if the temperature is too warm or too cold; and avoid chilled drinks such as cold waters, poultry broth, and venison, do not drink wine, nor consume any fatty foods, and do not overeat on meats that fill up the veins with blood, until you are certain there will be no hot abscess or discharge of matter from the limb; then follow the initial rest as is customary for such patients.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that cause heavy nutrition, such as cooked wheat in water, rice, beans, lentils, cheese, eggs, fresh fish, strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	Because with this kind of nutrebrightness the fractures heal quickly and faster.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	 And know that old and worn-out bones cannot be well joined or soldered according to their nature for the strengthening of limbs, nor those which are too flexible, like children's bones; but care is needed: reset on the broken bone with large supports so they align correctly, until it gains strength as if unbroken; and do not leave entirely without work, hence you must nourish with hearty meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are various in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	When a fracture of the head is different from that of the foot or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For some fractures go up to the head and others by sharpening, as writing with a pen tip.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, and a crack like a small tear.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	 And each condition requires its own method and proper instrument for restoration, as memory comes to mind in that place; and it is known the bone break by how much the marrow turns, and opens well from within, and near the pressing of the hand; and when there is no twisting or touching point, and the patient does not feel great pain unless there is a break. But it can well have twisting, or fracturing, or small breaks.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	But do not move the hand unless it is necessary; then apply medicines that come later in this manner and gently restrain now subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	 Know that the break which is in motion and the two parts disjoined should now be put back evenly, as with abscesses when they come forth; and if an abscess swells, leave it for no day until it is soothed; then make it level to movements you can ease lightly and soundly, knowing that the restoration of this will be easier than in those where pieces have been taken; then strain, as required afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	 And if in the bone there are broken pieces, whether they extend to two parts, be it hand or foot, or to your arm where small members are involved, or to strings, or to one string and your hand; then place the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the limb are disjointed, you reset them by all means back into their places with movements you can make, and ensure through your work that no injury or pain comes upon the patient; and properly align the two ends of the bone in their best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And if the hand feels quite well to you but not perfectly: dress it neatly and do not strain or press it as those who cause abscesses with heat and contraction of limbs, which we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	 And when the limb is at a point, so chastise it well that the patient does not move it, neither in waking nor sleeping, turning or any other way; and ensure the limb is secure enough to feel no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	 For when it feels no pain, then it is not at a point, and you must place it in such a position that it feels no pain; and ensure it is placed correctly, so twisting does not occur as it is restored; the quality of the broken limb follows what I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are of various sizes, both small and large, and forms.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	 For there are small members such as arms and legs and similar ones: wrap them with soft linen cloths; for larger ones like thighs and legs: use a wide and sturn d ring, because the wide rings encircle the entire large member equally, ensuring no part is left out, then tie around light pads three or four turns depending on the limb, and grip tightly with your hand all along the ring, then move to above the fracture and grip less, so that as the fracture moves a little further away; then gradually loosen the ring bit by bit until you grasp a large part of the healthy portion, then take another ring, and wrap neatly around again on top of the broken area; then return to above the fracture, grip moderately, not too hard or too soft as we have said in the first instruction above; then place linen pads between the rings until they are all even, then tie with a bandage three times, and then put well-made splints underneath, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	 If there is swelling or an abscess, apply a soothing ointment for the abscess and remove the swelling, leaving it as such for several days; then straighten your tools, which should be moistened with one hand breadth of linen cloth well rinsed, or wood from which clips are made, or palm fronds, shaped accordingly.
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	 But it is necessary that the stitch put on the break should be slightly larger and wider than the others; and just as long as needed for small or large limbs; then pull up the stitches as you did with the first incision, then above a thread at once, as in the first incision over the wound; thinner it becomes, closer together later on; and the thread should be medium, not too thick nor too thin, and made of fine linen. This is because if the threads are thick, like I have seen from peasants who make their rope cords with twisted flax, it's a great mistake, as the stitches cannot be equal if they are too subtle; thus, there should not be less than two finger widths of space between each stitch.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is in pain from the heads of the stones after resetting into healthy positions, place cotton or linen rags under them so they do not move.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by broken bones, I will explain its treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to strain all broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	 When the limb is large, it may not require placing splints unless after V days or VII days, depending on your certainty of an abscess occurring; and here's how ancient emplacements are used to restore broken bones, dislocations, and twists: take flour that adheres like mill walls with abundant egg white, making the mixture neither too clear nor too thick, using it in this manner is a common way for splints to mend fractures of various kinds, especially in women and small children, as it's not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of poultice for healing fractures and dislocations and twists: take pitch from the pine tree and tanydeum and olive oil and gum arabic and mastic resin, about 12 parts each; myrrh and aloeswood, about 5 parts each; frankincense .viiij. (7) parts; and make a powder, with honeycomb wax mixed with raw butter; if the patient's constitution is hot, use this poultice as it has good composition, and quickly restores broken bones, beneficial to many individuals.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	 Another splint method for twists: take mugwort and wormwood in ten ounces; thyme and aloes in nineteen ounces; rosemary six ounces; bolus Armeniac twenty ounces, pound well, mix with water or abundant egg white, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	 Another method of reducing joints and the bones from their place, relieves soreness arising, and those who break it, take new linens, and the meal in ease and boiled oil, and put them on top.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	 These plasters do not heal, but are good to soothe hot abscesses and properly alleviate pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method to mend broken bones: take dry leaves of fig, and leaves of earthly poppy, and grind them together, and make a paste.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	 Another method of healing the fracture of bone and to soothe those remaining with an abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	 Take root of valerian, chamomile, flowers of violets, wheat flour, from each one part; and grind it, and knead with wine, and if the limb is inflamed, then apply the poultice with moist coriander water or plain water, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	 Another method of incision more frequent than the first, when an abscess comes to heal the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	 Take roots of valerian and linseed, balm, mallows, and sage, as well as flowers of violets and chamomile, all equally mixed; grind them together with saltwater or fresh water, or wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras states in his book that nothing should be applied on a broken limb for healing other than wax and oil mixture, and it should not be too hard or too soft.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And according to Galen, one should apply dry and slightly warm substances on a broken limb for healing, such as myrrh, aloe, incense, and similar things, as we have mentioned.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method for dressing wounds and alleviating pain: take crushed dog and cat hairs or feathers from birds, as well as yarrow and equal amounts of the same herbs, then grind them together to create a poultice and apply it to the affected area.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then the patient should be left a while later, and take care if the patient does not feel any pain or has lost their place in their bones; do not reset it by hand for long days. If pain comes to the limb, or pruritus, a feeling of restlessness or swelling occurs quickly, then remove the incision now, and bandage gently, and use a moist sea sponge, and soak in water, and lift the affected area until the itching ceases and pain is alleviated; then let the limb rest for an hour, then apply a dry or oily poultice wrapped in cloth, as long as you are sure of heating. This will restore blood flow to the inflamed limb and relieve pain, then start again with gentle resetting and a small incision, but not too forcefully as before; continue gently until it is healthy.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that an abscess and redness and pain and swelling are throughout the bone, and you need opium and ligature, when it is resumed as before.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	 If none of the body part comes as we have said, do not reset it until after III days or IIII or V or VII; and never leave it unset for XX days, according to what is seen, as long as the breaker is sore, and approaches the joint above the cartilage; then you should relocate more securely than before, and swell the flesh, as I have said earlier; and if you see the place drying more than necessary, know that ulcerations cannot come about; therefore douse it with warm water each time you reset it, every day, and moisten slightly. Thus, you can prevent ulcers on the limb, and expedite healing as doctors would, who properly reposition the twisted body part: this is wrong, and such practices are fearsome, and I see nothing else but weakness and working directly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	 Many ways of breaks are found, and various shapes, and the causes are distinguished; for there are breaks caused by spear percussion, where the collar bone shatters all the bone up to the suture which is below the bone, as made by haft or handle; and for this reason it is called this type of fracture "haftage".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	When the sword cleaves the bone above without piercing, and this manner of fracture is called "absolute"; there are wounds from these two large or small fractures.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an impacted break, crack, or stone bruise, or from falling on stones, and similar injuries.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a sliding fracture, which reaches the skin just above or below the bone, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	 And if from a wound healed in the bone so subtle as hairs, and it is a small crack, and thusly called this fracture "capillary"; and if the wound caused by striking with an arrow, or falling, or similar thing, allows the piece of bone to protrude, and the openings above are like those of goldsmiths when they strike upon their furnaces; between the shards within.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	 And this occurs in those who have weak bones from excess moisture, as in children's skulls; and it happens in all manners of fractures where small pieces are dislodged similarly; and I will speak to them specifically.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all ways of bone fractures through displacement above them, and examination with probing rods, and by the decayed cartilage that is below.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair-like appearance is known when you have discovered the bone and rubbed it gently; then the bone fracture appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	by; and so.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an easily recoverable accident, but expect a cure, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the pain first reaches you, and it is in winter, one must remove the bone before the fourteenth day that you can move.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is thus (the situation), and you hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, then so that the tissue around the bone becomes corrupted, come the accidents that we have mentioned.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	 And if the bone fracture reaches just below the skin covering the brain, then you must cut into the separated part as follows: and take out the head piece that pains the patient, and reveal the bone in all ways possible, and on top of the wound's surface area, as much as you can; if bleeding occurs when exposing the bone or abscesses appear, use what is appropriate for this situation. And fill the cavity with stitched cloth soaked in rose oil; let the wound rest until the abscesses are relieved, and ensure that bleeding has stopped; then begin removing tissue around the bacteria: there are two ways of doing this operation: one method is to cut from a narrow area at the front, which is called excision.
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then he makes another incision larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is to have numerous incisions of different kinds, some narrow and others wide, pointed or made with an iron instrument; perform this work gently, without cutting the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is thick and hard, it must be pierced all around so that you make incisions with chisels without piercing through the skull, and there should be a margin or circle above the tip of each one to prevent the point from going beyond the bone; therefore, you should have several, so that each is placed according to the thickness of the bone, having chisels for all types of skulls; this is the form of the three methods of chisels:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	You place a vessel over the broken bone so you can feel when it is completely pierced; then move the vessel to another part for a while and do this throughout, then use scissors on the space between the fragments of bone as subtly as possible and gently, as we have said, until you reach the bone with your hand or any of the tools you have like pincers. And be careful not to touch the brain or spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	 When you have felt the bone and broken it, it is necessary to reset the readiness that has been delayed from the bone by all other instruments similar to a chisel; but it must be more secure and finer than the others; and if nothing of small bones or scales remain, gently wash with clean solutions; then treat the wound as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of treatment is that which Galen describes, which is more subtle; and let it be done strongly, as he says.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is first necessary to expose the part of the bone where the break occurred, and once it has been exposed, place atop the flat head of this chisel-like instrument, which looks like so:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	 And do not cut through it completely, and the area is weak in two sides, so that the cutting tool faces the bone; then strike gently with a small mallet from below, as to chip off the entire bone surface, taking care of the covering above; if it's soft near the bone, slightly move the bone without harming or causing fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not pierce through to the skin and the bone is cut above slightly, leaving small fragments; then apply care to that area, and use a fine razor to remove scales in varying amounts as needed for each location with the most suitable treatment according to the nature of the fracture and its shape.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If there are many large scales, first use more substantial tools, then transition to finer ones, and continue until it is thoroughly done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of these other hair treatments and delicate breaks, it is necessary to reset them according to their precise direction; and this is something that cannot be restored for those who have studied in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	 If the wound is discovered, you must take a linen bandage according to the size of the wound, anoint with oil roseate and place it on the wound; then take another doubled bandage made of II or III layers, anointed with wine and oil roseate and place it over the first bandage. Proceed as gently as possible so you do not burden the syphacus, then administer above the other linen the prescribed remedy, without straining it too much until only the wound is touched; leave in this manner for one or two days until the boil calms down, then remove and apply medicines as root of lily, flour of veils, powder of incense, aristology, and similar things. Make a powder from these substances, place it on the wound, and administer appropriate medicines without biting; ensure that the wound remains clean, not leaving any ointment or residue, as when bowels come together over the cervical cloth, they tangle and chafe, causing great distress. For when one puts a mordant on the syphacus, it irritates from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if by any chance something happens to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If only darkness comes due to the medicine applied and its power is not sufficient, then it is necessary that you mix a part of honey with three parts of roselle oil in one cloth rag, and apply it over the wound; then treat according to the appropriate methods until healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that at no time are the two bones above broken or severed by themselves alone, for they are both bone; and that below is cartilage, which does not break nor twist, but heals in due course.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	 And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you sew your small thumb or finger and place the torn part inside your index finger, then tie it off at the base with thread; let the nail grow back to its natural shape slowly, do this gently, and ensure the patient does not feel pain during the procedure.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is above the nail, and cannot bring the finger back to its original position, it's necessary that you align them even with a bit of force on one side.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	 And if the break is in two parts, repeat as before, and attempt to restore it by the first day; if not possible, after seven days or at most ten when the inflammation has subsided, then stitch together with linen cloth strips, if the tear is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you bind another on the other side, if the fracture is there; and let the linen cloths be so large that they fill the slits of the neck.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	 And some healers say that one must move the tentacles as if with butter, and change each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	 It seems to me it might not be entirely right, but one should soften them with a mixture of oil and egg, and powdered mill flour; then leave the tentacle until the bone is firm, and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	At no time are goose feathers blown into the tent openings, and if one is near an exposed sore, it becomes aggravated, causing a breeze that troubles the sickly person; thus do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes to the wound while you work on it, place a piece of lint or cotton soaked in rose oil, or a small amount of diaquilon (iodine).
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if an abscess does not come out, then apply a poultice afterward, of millet flour and incense powder, mixed with egg oil; then place it on light gauze and do not tie the edges; and if the bone break due to the abscess is small and broken into tiny pieces, extract as much pus as appropriate for this condition, then cut open the wound, and heal various things like charcoal, sulfur, and such poultices and ointments suitable for this; and if there are no injuries inside the bone, treat with tentacle dressing and apply plum extract until it is healthy.
de la routure de la mandibule	Regarding the treatment of a broken jawbone:
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is dislocated and there is no resulting wound or fracture present, and the breaks are slight only, unless cracks inside can be seen with ease.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary that if the fracture is on the right side, you insert your index finger into the patient's mouth; and if the fracture is on the left mandible, put your index finger of your right hand in it gently, align it carefully with the other hand slowly, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is dislocated at two points, it is necessary that you adjust the expansion so evenly.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	If movements of the teeth occur or jostling happens, then strain one with a thread of gold or silver or silk; place on the broken mandible cerot, and put on it a double cloth; lay a large well-made stone under the cloth, or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the mandible, at the junction you can see, and instruct the patient to rest, and consume light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the figure is changing, relocate the dislocated joint, and then restore what has changed; place a poultice over it with finely ground powder or wheat flour after removing the cerot; put on a light linen, and as long as the poultard remains, the patient's condition does not change; often it is cured in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses come about, treat them as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, no part of the bone has been set; subtly remove the fragments near the bruises with this tool.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, enlarge it with flame as needed.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.
